  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer16681254738061765500">East London, 1888 - a city apart. A place of shadow and light where thieves, whores, and dreamers mingle, where children play in the cobbled streets by day and a killer stalks at night, where bright hopes meet the darkest truths. Here, by the whispering waters of the Thames, Fiona Finnegan, a worker in a tea factory, hopes to own a shop one day, together with her lifelong </span>
  <span id="freeText16681254738061765500" style="display:none">East London, 1888 - a city apart. A place of shadow and light where thieves, whores, and dreamers mingle, where children play in the cobbled streets by day and a killer stalks at night, where bright hopes meet the darkest truths. Here, by the whispering waters of the Thames, Fiona Finnegan, a worker in a tea factory, hopes to own a shop one day, together with her lifelong love, Joe Bristow, a costermonger's son. With nothing but their faith in each other to spur them on, Fiona and Joe struggle, save, and sacrifice to achieve their dreams.<br /><br />But Fiona's life is shattered when the actions of a dark and brutal man take from her nearly everything-and everyone-she holds dear. Fearing her own death, she is forced to flee London for New York. There, her indomitable spirit propels her rise from a modest West Side shop-front to the top of Manhattan's tea trade. But Fiona's old ghosts do not rest quietly, and to silence them, she must venture back to the London of her childhood, where a deadly confrontation with her past becomes the key to her future.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Actually, none that I would call "sex". There is a bit of romance, but it is mainly a story of a woman who rises from working in a factory, to one of <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Actually, none that I would call "sex". There is a bit of romance, but it is mainly a story of a woman who rises from working in a factory, to one of the top competitors of Twining tea! It is such a charming story that will make you laugh, cry, and fall in love with Fiona. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=1800s">1800s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer165646913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10736960522251349269"><b>3.5 stars.</b> This book is not at all what I expected! I thought it was historical fiction, but there's too much crazy melodrama for it to be that. Then I thought it was a historical romance, but it's far too detailed and well done for that, too. So the book is either extremely campy historical fiction or really, really excellent historical romance. But either way, it's loads and loads of fun.<br/><br/>A few things you should know about me that factor into why I enjoyed this book so much:<br/><br/>* I am picky about m</span>
  <span id="freeText10736960522251349269" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars.</b> This book is not at all what I expected! I thought it was historical fiction, but there's too much crazy melodrama for it to be that. Then I thought it was a historical romance, but it's far too detailed and well done for that, too. So the book is either extremely campy historical fiction or really, really excellent historical romance. But either way, it's loads and loads of fun.<br /><br />A few things you should know about me that factor into why I enjoyed this book so much:<br /><br />* I am picky about my tea. I have a lot of tea accessories and I love the ritual of going to tea and eating elegant little sandwiches.<br />* I have a weakness for gorgeous gowns and ladies in big hats. I read lots of catalogues and fashion magazines.<br />* I own vintage gloves and handkerchiefs. I dart around flea markets looking for pretty brooches. I get Victorian Papers catalogue. <br />* I am somewhat obsessed with food. I read food blogs and tweets and magazines and cookbooks. I have a whole cupboard devoted to baking materials.<br /><br />That part of me, the girly romantic part who loves pretty fans and peonies and nesting, is the one who loves this book. The author writes wonderful descriptions that bring up the exotic scent of tea wafting up from a tin, the heartiness and comfort of a good hot meat pie, and the bustling activity on the teeming streets of London.<br /><br />The sensible part of me, the one who files her taxes in January and grits her teeth at the misuse of the term "literally," notes the following:<br /><br />* This book is wildly melodramatic and unrealistic and predictable.<br />* Every character is one-dimensional; they are either perfect or evil.<br />* There are too many POVs.<br />* The Jack the Ripper subplot is superfluous, as are some of the secondary characters and details.<br />* Far too many people die.<br />* There is too much name-dropping. (Yep, you can do that in a Victorian novel, as long as you include Gauguin and the Prince of Wales various other luminaries in your anecdotes.)<br />* There is an unfortunate tendency to jump forward in the story and then backtrack with a flashback.<br />* The author gives her characters a little too much credit in coming up with innovations in their fields.<br />* There are too many instances of telling us things about a character rather than showing them.<br />* Fiona is the ultimate Mary Sue with her beautiful face and figure, brilliant blue eyes, and tendency to strike awe and admiration in everyone she meets.<br /><br />Having said all that, however, I really started to like Fiona after she leaves London. In the beginning, she's just a willful, reckless teenager, but she gradually develops into a pretty strong and admirable woman. I also liked how she gradually builds her wealth through her ingenuity and enthusiasm (and lots of luck), as well as the master scheme she undertakes to take revenge on those who have done her wrong. <br /><br />I really liked the descriptiveness of the author's writing, particularly in regards to London and the day to day life of the working class. The author has a good ear for language and I enjoyed reading about the tea factory and the development of Fiona's tea trade, Joe's vegetable stand, and Fiona's little merchant shop. I am surprised that an author who writes so well in that regard, however, settles for such sketchy characterizations and overly dramatic plots. Fiona and Joe and Nicholas and so on are all likable, but none of them are very deep, and they all behave in ways that approach hysteria at times. I would also have liked to have seen Fiona achieve some measure of <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[personal fulfillment outside of her relationship with Joe. You shouldn't have to wait 10 years and cross an ocean to get to happiness. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>There are also far too many instances of "Look how wonderfully Fiona does <i>this</i>" types of passages. Editing these sorts of things could have easily turned this into a truly excellent work of historical fiction. <br /><br />Still, I was so entertained by this novel that I couldn't stop reading it. It's sort of like a Victorian soap opera--high camp, beautiful clothes and setting, and lots of fun. I wasn't at all surprised by any of the events that occurred or by any of the characters, but I was pleased by the time I spent with them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10736960522251349269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_42887210" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42887210" />
    <a title="Allison (The Allure of Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books"><img alt="Allison (The Allure of Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1247775031p2/1637878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/42887210?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison (The Allure of Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison (The Allure of Books)" href="/user/show/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books">Allison (The Allure of Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312993566" href="/book/show/937224.The_Tea_Rose">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer42887210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12263663729858851277">This book has faults. The story was pretty far fetched at times-but I suppose in kind of an endearing "fairy tale" way (which is funny, since a great deal of the book is extremely horrible and depressing), and the main character didn't really have any flaws.<br/><br/>Well, I take that back. Fiona, the main character, was in love with Joe. That is a fault, in my eyes. They grew up together, were in love, and had big plans to get rich together. Well, through a horrible chain of events, they ended up on oppo</span>
  <span id="freeText12263663729858851277" style="display:none">This book has faults. The story was pretty far fetched at times-but I suppose in kind of an endearing "fairy tale" way (which is funny, since a great deal of the book is extremely horrible and depressing), and the main character didn't really have any flaws.<br /><br />Well, I take that back. Fiona, the main character, was in love with Joe. That is a fault, in my eyes. They grew up together, were in love, and had big plans to get rich together. Well, through a horrible chain of events, they ended up on opposite continents. I'm not saying that what happened was really Joe's fault - the whole thing was so pathetic, I was mad at him at first but really just ended up being sorry for him - but I am not a member of Joe's fan club. He is alright, I just think Fiona is better then him. I forgave Donnelly for making Fiona so perfect - because really, she earned it. Bless her heart, she really got run through the mill in the story.<br /><br />Okay...now for the two main reasons I loved the book beyond all reason:<br /><br />1. Nicholas Soames. He is officially one of my favorite characters of all time. He DID have his flaws (spoiled rich kid), but bless his heart, he did not live an easy life. I fell in love with him, and so did Fiona (in a friendly way). Their close friendship and devotion to each other is one of the main reasons I forgive Fiona for being perfect. I cannot say enough that <u>I love this guy</u>. From the very second he walked into the story, I knew it was getting five stars. I felt such an emotional connection to him, I have never wanted to be friends with a character so much. Ever. He melted (and then broke) my heart.<br /><br />2. The book made me <i>feel</i>. Just a few words into Page 1, Donnelly put me into the story...she just makes you feel like you are right there. Once I was in, she never let up. I was a part of that story from beginning to end, and that is a gift. No matter what problems the plot might have, you cannot ignore an author - or a story - that so fully captures you. Her descriptions and words are gorgeous. Also...I cried like a baby at one point (obviously I'm not going to tell you why, but when you read the book - then we'll talk). I mean...I put the book down for a few minutes and just sobbed. A book hasn't done that to me in...I don't know how long. I felt silly, but I couldn't help it. The story broke my heart.<br /><br />There was a happy ending though, no worries. Don't let my crying put you off.<br /><br />This is a great story, it is a long one...but I really think it is worth the time. It, in many ways, isn't very original...but there are plenty of twists you won't see coming. It is a strange combination of Gaskell's North and South, Dumas' Count of Monte Cristo, and heck...I'll even through in the musical Rent. (Ha! If that isn't an intriguing combination, I don't know what is.) </span>
  <a data-text-id="12263663729858851277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_6809992" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6809992" />
    <a title="Renee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/419871-renee"><img alt="Renee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1261625354p2/419871.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6809992?book_show_action=true">Sep 25, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Renee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Renee" href="/user/show/419871-renee">Renee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No One I Actually Like</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6809992" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18004408783813510789">I had a lot of hope for this after reading Donnelly's "A Northen Light" (which I really liked) and after learning that "A Tea Rose" was set in London at the time of the Jack the Ripper murders (a very intriguing setting, I thought). But I'm sorry to say, I was terribly disappointed.<br/><br/>The characters are all extremely stale. Good-hearted and good-looking people who have unfortunately been born into the working class. There are no flaws to make them human. Nothing I could relate with. Plus, the bigge</span>
  <span id="freeText18004408783813510789" style="display:none">I had a lot of hope for this after reading Donnelly's "A Northen Light" (which I really liked) and after learning that "A Tea Rose" was set in London at the time of the Jack the Ripper murders (a very intriguing setting, I thought). But I'm sorry to say, I was terribly disappointed.<br /><br />The characters are all extremely stale. Good-hearted and good-looking people who have unfortunately been born into the working class. There are no flaws to make them human. Nothing I could relate with. Plus, the biggest fault of this book I think, is the unbelievability of it. Main characters Fiona and Joe, lovers separated by a horrible scheme (Fiona goes to New York, Joe stays in London), are dirt-poor but somehow, in a very short time, they both become extraordinarily rich on their own wit and intuition. Oh yes, it's completely believable that a factory worker and a costermonger in the late nineteenth century could BOTH rise up to the top of society in so short a time. <br /><br />Stereotypical characters. Predictable, illogical plotlines. Full of cliches. Sorry, Donnelly, only 1 star this time.<br /><br />Find more book reviews at <a href="http://www.aquickredfox.com" rel="nofollow noopener">A Quick Red Fox</a>.</span>

<div id="review_1063259700" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1063259700" />
    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9371994-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461856985p2/9371994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1063259700?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/9371994-allison">Allison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781429973090" href="/book/show/8130083-the-tea-rose">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=setting-1800s">setting-1800s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=own-physical-shelf">own-physical-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=series-complete">series-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=grim-gritty">grim-gritty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=romantic-elements">romantic-elements</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=setting-britain-ireland">setting-britain-ireland</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=romance-rating-adult-r">romance-rating-adult-r</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=jack-the-ripper">jack-the-ripper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=dark">dark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1063259700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17855365806744241338"><i>The Tea Rose</i> was a really good book, and I'm so glad I persevered past the absolutely devastating first 200-300-odd pages. It's one of those books that starts off with everything going so well that you know it's not going to last long. I had a sense of foreboding, but the amount of tragedy and pain was really too much. It just kept coming in wave after wave. It wasn't just a bit dark or a bit tragic. It was crushing, suffocating loss and pain. That's going to stick with me for a while. I'm reall</span>
  <span id="freeText17855365806744241338" style="display:none"><i>The Tea Rose</i> was a really good book, and I'm so glad I persevered past the absolutely devastating first 200-300-odd pages. It's one of those books that starts off with everything going so well that you know it's not going to last long. I had a sense of foreboding, but the amount of tragedy and pain was really too much. It just kept coming in wave after wave. It wasn't just a bit dark or a bit tragic. It was crushing, suffocating loss and pain. That's going to stick with me for a while. I'm really proud of myself for pushing through it, because I usually hate reading books full of tragedy, and this was darker than I can usually tolerate.<br /><br />I'm fairly certain I stuck with it partly because of the tea. I love tea. I drink it all day long. And I love Victorian stories, and this one was refreshingly focused on industry and shops, and factories - not something I've seen very often since packaging and selling tea is not as glamorous as taking tea in the parlor. The sense of place was very vivid, and it kept me reading, along with the hope that such tragedy couldn't continue for 700 pages without reprieve.<br /><br />I was totally ready to walk away if Part 2 didn't start turning things around. But luckily it did. From that point on, even though there are still sad parts, the overall tone is more hopeful, and things start to go right. I was finally able to settle down into an enjoyable historical tale with more regular ups and downs. The strength of love and friendships and resilience of spirit began to shine through, and the memory of those will stick with me for a while too. <br /><br />Then, for the last part of the book, I suddenly found myself glued to the pages. I couldn't read fast enough to see how everything would play out. I wasn't completely sure I could trust everything to work out how I wanted it to, but in the end, all of the resolutions were so completely satisfying. I can't believe I'm saying it, but it was worth it to persevere. What a roller coaster ride.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17855365806744241338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1544466487" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1544466487" />
    <a title="LENA TRAK" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51989964-lena-trak"><img alt="LENA TRAK" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531790695p2/51989964.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1544466487?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LENA TRAK" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LENA TRAK" href="/user/show/51989964-lena-trak">LENA TRAK</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51989964-lena-trak?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1544466487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11752082756371929565"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/261331.The_Tea_Rose__The_Tea_Rose___1_' title='The Tea Rose (The Tea Rose, #1) by Jennifer Donnelly' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Tea Rose</a> <br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/36346.Jennifer_Donnelly' title='Jennifer Donnelly' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jennifer Donnelly</a><br/><br/><i>“We're not punished for our sins, lad. We're punished by them.”<br/><br/>“God didn't have to punish him; he'd created his own hell. By himself and for himself.”</i><br/><br/>I don’t really know why I took so long to pick this book up. I guess I felt intimidated by its size. Also, having devoured “A Northern Light” I was afraid this one wouldn’t be equally good. Well, I can honestly say that I was captivated by its beautiful storyline. So don’t let the number of pages put you off.<br/><br/>The Tea Ro</span>
  <span id="freeText11752082756371929565" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/261331.The_Tea_Rose__The_Tea_Rose___1_" title="The Tea Rose (The Tea Rose, #1) by Jennifer Donnelly" rel="nofollow noopener">The Tea Rose</a> <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/36346.Jennifer_Donnelly" title="Jennifer Donnelly" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer Donnelly</a><br /><br /><i>“We're not punished for our sins, lad. We're punished by them.”<br /><br />“God didn't have to punish him; he'd created his own hell. By himself and for himself.”</i><br /><br />I don’t really know why I took so long to pick this book up. I guess I felt intimidated by its size. Also, having devoured “A Northern Light” I was afraid this one wouldn’t be equally good. Well, I can honestly say that I was captivated by its beautiful storyline. So don’t let the number of pages put you off.<br /><br />The Tea Rose tells the heartbreaking story of Fiona Finnigan who lives in the poor neighborhood of East End, London around the time of Jack the Ripper (late 1880s). After her family is destroyed by severe poverty and death Fiona flees London to start anew in New York. Propelled by strong desire for life and revenge, she manages to rise from the ashes and become a successful tea trader. But when the ghosts of her past return, she realizes it’s time to confront her deadly enemies.<br /><br />The book contains a number of historical references which makes it all the more interesting. The mystery surrounding the identity of Jack the Ripper, though is what made it impossible for me to put the book down. However, it would be amiss of me if I didn’t tell you how far-fetched the story gets sometimes. Absurd coincidences and utterly stupid decisions made by sane and benevolent characters had me question the book at times. However, once you accept the fact that this is a fictional story and allow yourself to get carried away by the enthralling narration you will love it. I surely did. <br /><br />The Tea Rose has everything. Romance, murder mystery, suspense, drama, revenge; all meticulously weaved around a carefully structured premise (though not so original) and vividly described by Donnelly’s impeccable writing skills. There is a chance you don’t love this book as much as I did but it’s definitely worth a try! If you are looking for a good revenge story then this is the book for you!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11752082756371929565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1251871214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1251871214" />
    <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen"><img alt="Helene Jeppesen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528006866p2/21992464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1251871214?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helene Jeppesen" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen">Helene Jeppesen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1251871214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5154572847413155796">I really like this book because it is a great story. Fiona, our main character, goes through so much struggle and so many changes, and because she's such a lovely character you can't help but cheer for her. She's stubborn, loyal and very intelligent and I quickly fell in love with her. This goes for most of the characters in this book: They were so easy to fall in love with while other characters were so easy to hate. <br/>I do think that this book has its flaws. It's very predictable and and contain</span>
  <span id="freeText5154572847413155796" style="display:none">I really like this book because it is a great story. Fiona, our main character, goes through so much struggle and so many changes, and because she's such a lovely character you can't help but cheer for her. She's stubborn, loyal and very intelligent and I quickly fell in love with her. This goes for most of the characters in this book: They were so easy to fall in love with while other characters were so easy to hate. <br />I do think that this book has its flaws. It's very predictable and and contains a lot of the elements you can expect from a coming-of-age story. I wasn't really surprised at any point (not until the very last pages), but the truth is I didn't really mind that much. I loved the way the story was going and I loved to read about Fiona and her changes till the end. This is a very long book, but at no point did I feel like it was dragging too much or that any pages could have been taken out of the story. <br />I think the best part about "The Tea Rose" was the romance. Jennifer Donnelly has created an intense relationship between Fiona and her beloved one and my eyes were glued to the pages whenever we hear about this romance. The worst thing about this book was its predictability which didn't really enhance the reading experience. Last but not least, I find it extremely funny how Jennifer Donnelly has a way with words. She likes to play with sounds and this book is no exception. The silly name "Tastea" was just too foolish for me to take seriously, but at least you could see that this was a book written by Jennifer Donnelly.<br />All in all, a great love story and coming-of-age book that will encapture you from beginning to end if you read it with an open heart and an open mind. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5154572847413155796" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_529392297" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/529392297" />
    <a title="Aoibhínn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5799885-aoibh-nn"><img alt="Aoibhínn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452957222p2/5799885.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/529392297?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aoibhínn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aoibhínn" href="/user/show/5799885-aoibh-nn">Aoibhínn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5799885-aoibh-nn?shelf=historical">historical</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer529392297&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer529392297" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15062846271906177181">Set in London, England during the late 19th Century, <i>The Tea Rose</i> tells the tale of Fiona Finnegan. Fiona is the spirited, ambitious daughter of an Irish dock worker. She longs to break free from the squalid lanes and alleys of Whitechapel, where she has grown up and now has a job in a tea factory. With the love of her life, Joe Bristow, Fiona dreams of escaping the poverty and opening her own tea shop. But one by one her dreams fall apart as her father is killed in a dock accident, Joe is seduc</span>
  <span id="freeText15062846271906177181" style="display:none">Set in London, England during the late 19th Century, <i>The Tea Rose</i> tells the tale of Fiona Finnegan. Fiona is the spirited, ambitious daughter of an Irish dock worker. She longs to break free from the squalid lanes and alleys of Whitechapel, where she has grown up and now has a job in a tea factory. With the love of her life, Joe Bristow, Fiona dreams of escaping the poverty and opening her own tea shop. But one by one her dreams fall apart as her father is killed in a dock accident, Joe is seduced by another woman, and her mother is viciously murdered – a suspected victim of Jack the Ripper. <br /><br />Devastated, her life in tatters, Fiona flees to New York City where she sets up home with her alcoholic uncle Michael. Slowly she builds his small grocery shop into a thriving business and tea house, and her new life flourishes. After ten years of hard work, she establishes herself as the head of her own powerful tea empire. But she cannot forget London – or Joe. Convinced that her father was murdered by his brutal employer, Fiona vows to seek revenge and ruin him once and for all. Making her way back to the streets of her impoverished childhood, Fiona must start her fight again. <br /><br /><i>The Tea Rose</i> is an extremely well-researched and well-written novel which is packed full of unexpected twists and turns throughout the story. I really enjoyed this novel. I thought this book was very gripping, intriguing and engrossing tale and I found it very hard to put it down for long. I couldn't wait to find out what happened next! The descriptions of Victorian London were very vivid and I found it very easy to picture how the city looked in the 1880's thanks to these. <br /><br />I fell in love with all the main characters. They were all so interesting, compelling and very well-developed, especially Fiona. She was such a fierce, strong, intelligent and brave character. The secondary characters were wonderful too. There were ones you love to love and ones you love to hate and I loved the way the author wove Jack the Ripper into the story.<br /><br />I absolutely enjoyed this book! As soon as I finished this novel I brought the sequel, <i>The Winter Rose</i>, on my Kindle and I'm really looking forward to reading it! I will definitely be reading more of Jennifer Donnelly books, apart from this series, too sometime in the near future. <br /><br /><br /><b>Four Stars! </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15062846271906177181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2655763-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1250989196p2/2655763.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174042449?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312378028" href="/book/show/1306948.The_Tea_Rose">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2655763-lauren?shelf=books-i-want-to-burn">books-i-want-to-burn</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174042449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7479602249631976000">Although <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1306948.The_Tea_Rose__The_Tea_Rose___1_' title='The Tea Rose (The Tea Rose, #1) by Jennifer Donnelly' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Tea Rose</a> is not the worst book I've read, it's pretty terrible. With a good 200 pages of drivel, it raises the question, how did this slip past the editor? <br/><br/>The other 350 pages drift somewhere along a mediocre plot-line, ridiculous dialogue and predictable, fairytale-like situations. Every time a character had a setback in life it was magically resolved by some farfetched coincidence. The book was littered with long descriptions that add very little to the story. On page 13, Donnelly</span>
  <span id="freeText7479602249631976000" style="display:none">Although <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1306948.The_Tea_Rose__The_Tea_Rose___1_" title="The Tea Rose (The Tea Rose, #1) by Jennifer Donnelly" rel="nofollow noopener">The Tea Rose</a> is not the worst book I've read, it's pretty terrible. With a good 200 pages of drivel, it raises the question, how did this slip past the editor? <br /><br />The other 350 pages drift somewhere along a mediocre plot-line, ridiculous dialogue and predictable, fairytale-like situations. Every time a character had a setback in life it was magically resolved by some farfetched coincidence. The book was littered with long descriptions that add very little to the story. On page 13, Donnelly spends an entire paragraph detailing how Kate prepared dinner. It's no wonder the book is over 500 pages long.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Frowning, Kate banged the whisk on the side of the bowl, knocking globs of cream-colored batter from its wires, then tossed it in the sink. She picked up a fork and poked it into one of the three mutton chops sizzling on top of the stove. A rivulet of juice ran down the side of the chop, sputtering into steam as it hit the hot metal of the frying pan. She speared the chops, dropped them onto a plate, and put them into a warming hatch next to the oven, alongside a jug of onion gravy. Next she picked up a rope of sausages and cut the links into the pan. As they began to fry, she sat down at the table across from her husband."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The most annoying thing of all: Donnelly would spend hundreds of those pages leading up to the climax of a sub-plot, then she'd skip over it altogether and the reader would come in after. It was a huge letdown. The dialogue I did care enough to anticipate was skimmed over, leaving the reader with a sentence like, "Fiona told him the story of what had happened to her." Oh, great, thanks for that. <br /><br />Having read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64481.A_Northern_Light" title="A Northern Light by Jennifer Donnelly" rel="nofollow noopener">A Northern Light</a> as a teenager, I thought I would enjoy Jennifer Donnelly's adult fiction just as well. I was wrong.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7479602249631976000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16176818820552920830">East London 1888 is a place where in its shadows thieves, whores and dreamers mingle.<br/><br/>Fiona Finnegan works in a tea factory. She hopes to own her own shop one day along with her lifelong love, Joe Bristow. Fiona &Joe struggle, save and sacrifice to achieve their dreams.<br/><br/>Then Fiona's life is shattered when a brutal man takes nearly everything and everyone she holds dear. Fearing for her life she flees London and goes to New York. But Fiona's old ghosts do not rest easily and she has to return to Lo</span>
  <span id="freeText16176818820552920830" style="display:none">East London 1888 is a place where in its shadows thieves, whores and dreamers mingle.<br /><br />Fiona Finnegan works in a tea factory. She hopes to own her own shop one day along with her lifelong love, Joe Bristow. Fiona &amp;Joe struggle, save and sacrifice to achieve their dreams.<br /><br />Then Fiona's life is shattered when a brutal man takes nearly everything and everyone she holds dear. Fearing for her life she flees London and goes to New York. But Fiona's old ghosts do not rest easily and she has to return to London to face a deadly confrontation.<br /><br />A fantastic read. So well written with believable characters. A period drama with a mix of good and evil.<br /><br />I would like to thank NetGalley, Bloomsbury Publishing PLC (UK &amp; ANZ) and the author Jennifer Donnelly for my ARC in exchange for an honest review.</span>

<div id="review_1312677845" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1312677845" />
    <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma"><img alt="PattyMacDotComma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577835191p2/1128612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1312677845?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PattyMacDotComma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PattyMacDotComma" href="/user/show/1128612-pattymacdotcomma">PattyMacDotComma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1128612-pattymacdotcomma?shelf=aa-ce">aa-ce</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1312677845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10296683203082041810">I stumbled across The Tea Rose when looking for a book with Winter in the title and found The Winter Rose. Since that was part of a trilogy, I figured I'd skip the 'winter' challenge and try the first in the series - historical novel, lots of good reviews, sounded like fun.<br/><br/>Mostly, it was a pretty good read. Vivacious, irrepressible teen from a desperately poor family in Jack the Ripper's Whitechapel, loves, loses, suffers, faces murders, deaths, harrowing experiences, and heartbreak. Eventually </span>
  <span id="freeText10296683203082041810" style="display:none">I stumbled across The Tea Rose when looking for a book with Winter in the title and found The Winter Rose. Since that was part of a trilogy, I figured I'd skip the 'winter' challenge and try the first in the series - historical novel, lots of good reviews, sounded like fun.<br /><br />Mostly, it was a pretty good read. Vivacious, irrepressible teen from a desperately poor family in Jack the Ripper's Whitechapel, loves, loses, suffers, faces murders, deaths, harrowing experiences, and heartbreak. Eventually pretty satisfying. <br /><br />The story moves between London and New York at the end of the 19th century, but some of the words and phrases sounded too modern. My 'research' indicates they are anachronisms, but maybe nobody else minds, so I won't spoil it here.<br /><br />The pace is a little uneven, with a lot happening during the first year to year and a half of the story, when Fiona is 17 and 18, with good descriptions of life then. But major changes occur in unreasonably short periods of time. Drunks are reformed, buildings are renovated and restored, businesses are established - almost instantly - and all when she's still 18. But it's entertaining enough to keep me going to the end. <br /><br />I have to agree with other reviewers who've complained about spelling with dropped aitches for the Cockney accent. I know why the author has done it, and I have no alternative to offer.<br /><br />It's very readable, but too long, and I did get impatient with being told what a person was like rather than shown. I kept being told that people did what Fiona wanted because . . . whatever. force of personality? Beautiful young girl? I'd rather have the scene and the dialogue show me how she affects people and how they react. <br /><br />If you like historical romances and long books, this might be for you. I think I'll give the next two a miss.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10296683203082041810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12955485766545286683" style="display:none">Farting through silk dresses. That's what the uncle of the heroine says she'll be doing if she marries the rich man. Isn't that a great expression? And sadly, I've got nowhere to use it. Not unless I want even more bewildered looks than usual. This novel has been out for a decade now, and the fact that it's the choice of the History Fictionistas series read right now, speaks to its sticking power. And the centre of it is Fiona Finnegan, a feisty female fond of flavorful tea and fighting for family and friends. Her story begins in Whitechapel in the late 19th century, sails over to New York and then ten years later, returns to the shores of her homeland. It's got your star-crossed romance, your gay best friend, a serial killer, Dickensian lowlifes and a grand finale. A Winter Rose, the second in the series, is up next, and I'll be all over it. It features another tough heroine. I'm weak for strong women.</span>

    <a title="Cam *tactile seeker*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9924828-cam-tactile-seeker"><img alt="Cam *tactile seeker*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595916030p2/9924828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/346893300?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cam *tactile seeker*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cam *tactile seeker*" href="/user/show/9924828-cam-tactile-seeker">Cam *tactile seeker*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer346893300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14214460086976162704"><br/><b>*Spoilers*</b><br/><br/>One of the most disappointing books I've ever read.<br/><br/>I chose it among hundreds at the bookstore, immediately captivated by its beautiful cover and interesting blurb and ended up cursing at every single character repeatedly. They're all dull, incredibly stupid, even more incredibly childish and whiny. <br/>It's never their fault, but all their misfortunes always depend on someone else, on something else. They don't fight for their lives, they use other people in order to achieve their goals. I</span>
  <span id="freeText14214460086976162704" style="display:none"><br /><b>*Spoilers*</b><br /><br />One of the most disappointing books I've ever read.<br /><br />I chose it among hundreds at the bookstore, immediately captivated by its beautiful cover and interesting blurb and ended up cursing at every single character repeatedly. They're all dull, incredibly stupid, even more incredibly childish and whiny. <br />It's never their fault, but all their misfortunes always depend on someone else, on something else. They don't fight for their lives, they use other people in order to achieve their goals. I despise Fiona, in the 600+ pages I didn't find a single redeeming quality about her.<br />Crying and cursing over her boyfriend and the evil bitch (can't remember her name) who ruined her "perfect" love life, she basically whores herself for money, making us believe she's in love, and breaks the heart of the only man who was honest with her since the beginning.<br /><br />As for Joe, her "love", I despise him even more. He is forced to marry the aforementioned bitch who "traps" him by getting him drunk and taking him to her room, seducing him, (that part is so hilariously lame that even the mere thought still cracks me up. It's been 3 or 4 years since I've read it, but from what I still remember, she strips and ambushes him in the dark, playing the "he's too intoxicated and horny to refuse me" card and he fucks her like a rabbit, thoroughly enjoying the whole 30 seconds of the messy and ridiculous coupling) and ending up pregnant. <br /><br />There I said it, I've been waiting for years to finally write it down. It was disturbing and annoying, not to mention cruel and embarrassing.<br /><br />Joe and Fiona had just made love for the first time a day earlier, and knowing that the bitch wanted him and was scheming to make him marry her, he gets drunk at her party and fucks her like the horny teenager he really is. I was so disappointed and furious at that part that it really ruined everything else for me. <br /><br />It didn't help that Fiona behaved just like him in a couple of occasions. They both were like puppets, taking stupid actions without pondering them, not even for a minute, but being so lucky in the end, to end up rich and happy together again. <br /><br />AH, what a joy!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14214460086976162704" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText932874070739615665" style="display:none">When I first started reading this book, I thought "whew...over 500 pages. What kind of story are they trying to tell me? Is it going to be stuffed with description upon description of everything the main charactors come in contact with?" After finishing it, I could have read another 100 pages of the lives of Fiona and Joe. It was a book of second chances and missed opportunities. As well as a "I didn't see that coming and a yup that's what I figured" Loved it!<br /><br />Favorite quote...."We're not punished for our sins, but by them."</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3706714476495500038">The Tea Rose deserves an eloquently written review but honestly I don't think I'm able to write one worthy of it. It was one of the best books I've ever read and listened to and it will be an all time favorite of mine.   <span id="freeText3706714476495500038" style="display:none">The Tea Rose deserves an eloquently written review but honestly I don't think I'm able to write one worthy of it. It was one of the best books I've ever read and listened to and it will be an all time favorite of mine. The characters were simply fabulous and I felt as though I was actually part of the story— the author's writing was so compelling and real. It is a very long book yet I didn't want it to end. Thankfully there are two more equally long books in the series. I highly recommend this one. </span>

<div id="review_177632563" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177632563" />
    <a title="Doug Bradshaw" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/808994-doug-bradshaw"><img alt="Doug Bradshaw" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548429066p2/808994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177632563?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doug Bradshaw" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doug Bradshaw" href="/user/show/808994-doug-bradshaw">Doug Bradshaw</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer177632563&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177632563" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2600723379424483961">Well lads, and mainly lasses, I loved this book and it was almost five stars for me. I think if you classify it as a romance novel, it is a five star book. Here are some random thoughts and comments:<br/><br/>1. As another person said in her review, there were quit a few instances of the infamous Deus ex Machina where things are a little too convenient. And yet, not horribly so. To name a few, the way Fiona quickly found Nick and was able to get out of London. The Five Hundred Pounds that accidentally sho</span>
  <span id="freeText2600723379424483961" style="display:none">Well lads, and mainly lasses, I loved this book and it was almost five stars for me. I think if you classify it as a romance novel, it is a five star book. Here are some random thoughts and comments:<br /><br />1. As another person said in her review, there were quit a few instances of the infamous Deus ex Machina where things are a little too convenient. And yet, not horribly so. To name a few, the way Fiona quickly found Nick and was able to get out of London. The Five Hundred Pounds that accidentally showed up in her pocket, the estate she inherited from Nick owned a huge chunk of Burton Tea, etc. However, every one of them could've happened, right? And, why work so hard to make things happen? This device moved the story along at a good pace.<br /><br />2. There was a real romance and although somewhat corny (aren't they all?) it worked for me and I loved it and couldn't wait to see if the two would ever get back together. YESSS!!! I thought the physical encounters were fairly tastefully done and yet had some pretty good steam on them and I had to mop my brow a couple of times. The whole stupidity of a young guy getting drunk, having sex with the wrong person and then being punished for eternity, is miserable. But it really happens. Haven't we all done stupid rash things we get punished for? The continued devotion both had for each other was extremely touching and romantic. As a wizened old guy, I could be a little hard on that concept, but I won't because it got me and I liked it.<br /><br />3. Makes you want to go out and get rich by building a great little business, doesn't it? Of course, just look at the Waltons.<br /><br />4. I loved the setting in London and NYC in the late 1890's. I think she did some pretty good research about Jack the Ripper (a good goal for a lot of young writers but becoming a little overdone now?), the food, the men's clubs, the housing, the clothing, the accents and the gossip columnists, the police, the terrible disease of syphilis, the whole thing. <br /><br />5. The many characters who played minor roles from her brothers, her father and mother, Joe's family, Will, her wealthy suitor (I'm glad that worked out how it did), her gay husband Nick, the horrible Mr. Burton (maybe too creepy?) and that darn Millie, were all interesting and well thought out. I could almost see this shortened and done in a Broadway play. Wouldn't that be fun?<br /><br />Jennifer Donnelly is a great story teller. I was drawn into the story quickly and enjoyed it all of the way through. Thanks to the group I used to belong to who recommended it to me!<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="2600723379424483961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1815530712345554725">Loved the history, mystery, romance, murder, and family connections.<br/><br/>Loved this book...the characters are unforgettable....Fiona Finnegan comes from a poor family and works in the tea factory just like the rest of her family. Circumstances cause her to leave London and she becomes a "tea baron" - filled with history, love, importance of family, and a strong female heroine.<br/><br/>The sequel, THE WINTER ROSE, is just as unforgettable...the family legacy continues in this book.<br/></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5788507-melodie?shelf=contermporary-fiction">contermporary-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer227837530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15524274619258137123"> Fiona Finnegan is bright, outspoken and has big dreams. She is also one of the working poor in the part of London called ironically called Whitecastle. There is nothing white or royal about it.Life is not for the faint of heart in this and many other sections of 1888 London.<br/> But Fiona and her childhood sweetheart,Joe Bristow have big plans. They are going to have their own shop.They religiously squirrel little bits of money away against the day when they can break out of poverty into better liv</span>
  <span id="freeText15524274619258137123" style="display:none"> Fiona Finnegan is bright, outspoken and has big dreams. She is also one of the working poor in the part of London called ironically called Whitecastle. There is nothing white or royal about it.Life is not for the faint of heart in this and many other sections of 1888 London.<br /> But Fiona and her childhood sweetheart,Joe Bristow have big plans. They are going to have their own shop.They religiously squirrel little bits of money away against the day when they can break out of poverty into better lives.<br /> Life however has other plans and heart break ensues with the deaths of pretty much every member of Fiona's family with the exception of her youngest brother, and losing Joe to another girl.<br /> When Fiona overhears that her beloved father's death was not an accident but cold blooded murder, she finds herself along with her little brother running for her life.She survives and thrives in the life she fashions for herself. But she is driven by hurt and a deep rage at what has been stolen from her. Revenge will be hers...some day.<br /> This story put me in mind of the <b> A Woman of Substance</b> saga. I loved that series and I feel that this series will steal my heart as well.</span>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_148448884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/148448884" />
    <a title="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews"><img alt="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603380977p2/4863162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/148448884?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)" href="/user/show/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews">Jessie  (Ageless Pages Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=coverlove">coverlove</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=dramamongering">dramamongering</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=a-marysue-by-any-other-name">a-marysue-by-any-other-name</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=series-completed">series-completed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=i-cant-fight-this-feeeeling-anymore">i-cant-fight-this-feeeeling-anymore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=hf-england">hf-england</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4863162-jessie-ageless-pages-reviews?shelf=super-sized-story">super-sized-story</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer148448884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13172739089977232697"><b>Read <a href='http://agelesspagesreviews.blogspot.com/2011/06/review-tea-rose-by-jennifer-donnelly.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Review</a> & More Like It <a href='http://agelesspagesreviews.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>On My Blog</a>!</b><br/><br/>This is going to be an interesting review. But that is entirely fitting since this was an <i>interesting</i> book. I went back and forth on the rating of this as well. It's truly not good enough for more than a 3 star rating and yet, in the end, I sped through it and loved it. This also might end up being a tad bit more spoilery than I usually try to be; I honestly couldn't help it. This was part daytime soap-opera distilled into book form, part historical fic</span>
  <span id="freeText13172739089977232697" style="display:none"><b>Read <a href="http://agelesspagesreviews.blogspot.com/2011/06/review-tea-rose-by-jennifer-donnelly.html" rel="nofollow noopener">This Review</a> &amp; More Like It <a href="http://agelesspagesreviews.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">On My Blog</a>!</b><br /><br />This is going to be an interesting review. But that is entirely fitting since this was an <i>interesting</i> book. I went back and forth on the rating of this as well. It's truly not good enough for more than a 3 star rating and yet, in the end, I sped through it and loved it. This also might end up being a tad bit more spoilery than I usually try to be; I honestly couldn't help it. This was part daytime soap-opera distilled into book form, part historical fiction set in London/New York in 1880s/1890s, <i>The Tea Rose</i> is one hell of a fun, epic melodrama. We've got truly star-crossed lovers, decades-long revenge plots, sham marriages, murder plots, dockworker's union strikes, crooked politicians, Jack the Ripper, falling in love with New York millionaires, famous celebrity cameos, and of course, betrayal and redemption. <br /><br />There is a LOT of story going on here. I might sound critical, and I should; this book is not without a myriad of faults. Fiona, the main character, though likable, starts out as a bit of a Mary Sue cliche. She can be irritatingly overemotional and jealous in the beginning. Those annoying traits are stamped out quickly, however. Once she loses her father and her innocence, Fiona can finally find her own strength. Her enemy, the ruthless tea merchant behind her father's death, William Burton is chilling, though one dimensional. Regardless of the sheer outrageousness of the plot, shallowness of various characters and all the deux ex machinas, I <b>loved</b> this novel. It does have several things going for it: Donnelly spent numerous years researching her time period and culture of the Whitechapel area of London. Her descriptions of bleak and beautiful London were vivid, well-written and best of all, authentic. There was definitely the feel of 19th century present throughout the book. Ms. Donnelly managed to create an enthralling, absorbing atmosphere I had a hard time pulling myself away from. <br /><br />Everything in this novel is done on a grand scale. Fiona needs hardship? Check - half her family is murdered <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(all, eventually it turns out at the machinations of Jack the Ripper!) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. She needs an epic love that is tested? Check - Joe and Fiona are separated <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ FOR TEN YEARS. With NUMEROUS and frequent near misses. It's comical. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Fiona wants to have a business? Check - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she has the BIGGEST tea business in the United States <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />While the over-the-topness can be fun and work for the novel (such as getting Fiona out on her own and develop into a real character instead of a Mary Sue), it can also detract from the essentials. For instance, in this novel our intrepid heroes/heroines meet: Jack the Ripper (and have personal business with), the Crown Prince of Wales of England (Albert Edward), Paul Gaugin, Vincent van Gogh, Henri de Toulouse-Lautrec, and numerous other famous personages frequented Nick's idyllic life in Paris. Fiona's closest friend Nick, in addition to being the heir of the bank controlling Fiona's nemesis's company (though Nick and Fiona are unaware of this the <b>entire</b> time [10 years!!] they're friends) ends up being Viscount Elgin, firstborn son of the Duke of Winchester. That was all a bit much. Fiona has ridiculous luck once she arrives in America <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(Nick gets her on the boat, a famous New York millionaire steps in o help her, falls in love with her, she "invents" iced tea and tea packets, etc) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>; she has to in order to set her revenge against the men who killed her father. This made the book seem a bit rushed once Fiona and Seamie fled England. Also not helping the narrative were the random jumps of time between the three parts. Part Two to Part Three had an intervening nine years, in which crucial events to the story happen. Instead of showing Fiona build her business, her marriage, her revenge, it is simply "told" away in the beginning of the next part. I couldn't help but feel a bit cheated at that.<br /><br />Sadly, parts of the novel, though fun and campy, were entirely too predictable. Michael's recovery from alcoholism so rapidly and easily, Will McClane's swooping in to save Fiona's shop and proposing, his crooked son politician plotting against Fiona, the list goes on. I laughed a lot and often at this book. The only problem is that I am not sure I am laughing <i>at</i> the author/book or <i>with</i> them, where intended. <br /><br />Straining credulity, and poetic license aside (William Burton, Fiona's own personal foe was really Jack the Ripper? Really? That's where you went with that superfluous plotline?), I enjoyed this novel. It is not perfect, not even close. It's a melodramatic, over-the-top, romance-novelish tome of crazy. It's also a lot of fun. And the cover is pretty. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13172739089977232697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1774372-amy-bruno?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39697215" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6892796217345042285">I loved, loved, loved this book! The Tea Rose is a fabulous story of an amazing, ambitious girl, Fiona, from the slums of Whitechaple who dreams of a life without poverty and a boy named Joe. Fiona and Joe grew up with each other and are very much in love. Their relationship changes when Joe moves to a better job and then Fiona loses her family tragically and escapes to New York taking her 5-year-old brother, Seamie, with her. The story then follows Fiona’s life and struggles in New York and her</span>
  <span id="freeText6892796217345042285" style="display:none">I loved, loved, loved this book! The Tea Rose is a fabulous story of an amazing, ambitious girl, Fiona, from the slums of Whitechaple who dreams of a life without poverty and a boy named Joe. Fiona and Joe grew up with each other and are very much in love. Their relationship changes when Joe moves to a better job and then Fiona loses her family tragically and escapes to New York taking her 5-year-old brother, Seamie, with her. The story then follows Fiona’s life and struggles in New York and her rise to the top of the Tea trade. <br /><br /><br />Donnelly includes many wonderful characters throughout the book, my particular favorite being Nick. Fiona is a very interesting woman to read about, you really get to know her and you kinda miss her when you’re done. The relationship with her and Joe is beautiful and pure – you just know they are meant for each other. <br /><br /><br />All in all this is fabulous story telling and I highly recommend it to any lover of fiction. I mean this book has everything you could want: mystery, romance, power struggles, murder, grief, heartbreak, love…all the essentials!!!<br /><br /><br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer36960710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2812887327495346955">This was such a wonderful tale, I simply could not put it down. A tale of two star crossed lovers (they came SO CLOSE to finding each other time after time after time I wanted to scream!), a lovely glimpse of Victorian England and New York City. Many memorable characters, heartbreak and laughter and of course a truly evil villain waiting for the good guys to vanquish, and a surprise return from the dead at the end. Can't wait to read the sequel now. <br/><br/>My only complaints are just a few too many fam</span>
  <span id="freeText2812887327495346955" style="display:none">This was such a wonderful tale, I simply could not put it down. A tale of two star crossed lovers (they came SO CLOSE to finding each other time after time after time I wanted to scream!), a lovely glimpse of Victorian England and New York City. Many memorable characters, heartbreak and laughter and of course a truly evil villain waiting for the good guys to vanquish, and a surprise return from the dead at the end. Can't wait to read the sequel now. <br /><br />My only complaints are just a few too many famous people popping in and out of Fee's life in New York, and the reveal on the supposed identity of Jack the ripper was a bit over the top, but that's just splitting hairs. If you love Victorian England, true love and maybe a good cry or two, don't pass this up. And thank you Amazon for recommending items and a HUGE thanks to all those Listmania writers -- I would never have found this book or so many others that have enriched my life in the last year or so. </span>
